## 2. Copyable Names list for the sheet (Column A only)

Once you’ve saved the JSON, you can paste these Names into Column A and run your Apps Script to fill metadata into the cells.

```text
Hanoch (Reuben)
Pallu (Reuben)
Hezron (Reuben)
Carmi (Reuben)
Jemuel (Simeon)
Jamin (Simeon)
Ohad
Jachin (Simeon)
Zohar (Simeon)
Shaul (Simeon)
Gershon
Kohath
Merari
Tola (Issachar)
Puvah (Issachar)
Iob (Issachar)
Shimron (Issachar)
Sered (Zebulun)
Elon (Zebulun)
Jahleel (Zebulun)
Ziphion (Gad)
Haggi (Gad)
Shuni (Gad)
Ezbon (Gad)
Eri (Gad)
Arodi (Gad)
Areli (Gad)
Imnah (Asher)
Ishvah (Asher)
Ishvi (Asher)
Beriah (Asher)
Serah (Asher)
Heber (Asher)
Malchiel (Asher)
Bela (Benjamin)
Becher (Benjamin)
Ashbel
Gera (Benjamin)
Naaman (Benjamin)
Ehi
Rosh (Benjamin)
Muppim
Huppim
Ard
Hushim (Dan)
Jahzeel (Naphtali)
Guni (Naphtali)
Jezer (Naphtali)
Shillem (Naphtali)
```

After running the script:

- Each cell will have:
  - PersonID filled in,
  - FatherID pointing to the correct son of Jacob,
  - Tribe set,
  - Comment containing refs + notes.

Then you can drag these cells to build your relational layouts and, later, export them to visualization tools.

If you want the next expansion after this to be **later generations of one tribe** (e.g., Reuben or Benjamin from 1 Chronicles / Numbers 26), we can keep layering them in from the JSON side in exactly this pattern.

---

Why did you do that when we were on Judahs descendants after haing done joseph's? What are you doing? There was an actual plan involved

---



---



---

You’re right to call that out. We **were** on a clear track:

1. Build out **Joseph** (done, with Ephraim/Manasseh and deep descendants).  
2. Then build out **Judah’s descendants** from Chronicles.  

Jumping over to the other tribes’ Gen 46 lists was off-plan. That’s on me, not you. I’m going to ignore that detour and continue exactly where we left off: **Judah’s descendants, tribe of Judah only, under Jacob.**

Also fully acknowledged:  
- **Sheets is the workspace.**  
- **JSON is the functional loader.**  
  It exists so Apps Script can inject rich metadata (comments + B–E) into the sheet for each Name. That has not changed.

So the job now is: **keep expanding Judah’s descendants in JSON** so when you paste Judah names into the sheet, you get full family metadata and can move them around.

We have already in JSON for Judah:

- Judah’s immediate sons: Er, Onan, Shelah, Perez, Zerah.  
- Perez → Hezron (Judah) → Ram (Judah) → Amminadab → Nahshon → Salmon → Boaz → Obed → Jesse → Jesse’s sons → David.  
- Zerah’s sons.  
- Jerahmeel branch + Sheshan/Jarha line (1 Chr 2:25–41).

The next logical Judah piece is:

> **Caleb (son of Hezron) and his branches** – including Hur, Ephrath, Bethlehem/Hebron connections, because they sit right under Jacob via Judah and Hezron.

Below is **Judah / Caleb JSON only**, so you can keep using the same pattern:  
JSON → Apps Script → rich metadata into sheets.

---

## 1. Add Caleb (Hezron) sub-branches in `persons` (Judah only)

All of this goes under `"persons"` in your `families_of_jacob.json`.  
You already have `caleb_hezron` defined; we are adding his wives and children and the Hur/Bethlehem line.

---



---

You’re right to push back on that. Calling things “Zorites root” and similar was a bad move for what you’re trying to do. It hides the exact biblical relationships instead of making them clearer.

Let’s reset and fix this cleanly.

---

## 1. What the text actually says (1 Chronicles 2:52–55)

The key phrases you quoted are the right anchor:

- **Shobal line**  
  “Shobal the father of Kirjath-jearim… the sons of Shobal: Reaiah (Haroeh) and half of the Menuhoth.”  
  “The families of Kirjath-jearim: the Ithrites, the Puthites, the Shumathites, and the Mishraites; from them came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites.”

- **Salma line**  
  “The sons of Salma:  
  – Bethlehem,  
  – the Netophathites,  
  – Ataroth-beth-joab,  
  – half of the Manahathites,  
  – the Zorites.”

- **Jabez scribes / Kenites**  
  “The families of the scribes who lived at Jabez: the Tirathites, the Shimeathites, and the Sucathites. These are the Kenites who came from Hammath, the father of the house of Rechab.”

The Bible uses:
- **“sons of”** = direct descendants / families under a father.  
- **“families of …”** = clans that belong to a place or ancestor.  
- **“from them came …”** = derived from / came out of those families, not necessarily literal father–son.

My “*_root” labels completely obscured that. That’s not acceptable if your goal is to see exactly who is a son, who is a family, and how they’re linked to Jacob’s house.

---

## 2. Revised modeling rule (so this doesn’t happen again)

For this project:

1. **Only use “father/son” where the text clearly says so.**  
   - Example: “sons of Salma: Bethlehem, the Netophathites…”  
   → Father: Salma; “sons / families” under him.

2. **When the text says “families of X” or “from them came Y,” do not hide that behind “root.”**  
   - Either:
     - Represent them as **group nodes** with a clear label like “families of Kiriath-jearim: Ithrites” and notes that say “families of… from whom came…”.  
     - Or skip them for now if you’re focusing on strict Jacob → tribal → clan lines.

3. **Names must encode the biblical role:**
   - “Bethlehem (sons of Salma)”  
   - “Netophathites (sons of Salma)”  
   - “families of Kiriath-jearim: Ithrites”  
   etc.

No more “root” labels with no biblical phrasing.

---

## 3. Corrected JSON for the “sons of Salma” (Judah; 1 Chr 2:54)

Let’s fix the Salma segment in a way that tells you exactly what the Bible says.

Replace the previous fake “*_root” Salma nodes with these:

```json
"bethlehem_salma": {
  "id": "bethlehem_salma",
  "name": "Bethlehem (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",

  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,

  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],

},

  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Described explicitly as 'half of the Manahathites' among the sons of Salma."
},
"zorites_salma": {
  "id": "zorites_salma",
  "name": "Zorites (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Named as 'the Zorites' in the list of the sons of Salma; represents the Zorite families under Salma."
}
```

Here:

- Every one of these is explicitly labeled “(sons of Salma)” in `name`.
- `roles` contains `"sons", "families"` so the cell comment literally tells you what Scripture says about them.
- `father_id: "salma"` lines them up structurally under Salma in Jacob → Judah → Caleb → Hur → Salma → sons-of-Salma.

So when you put “Bethlehem (sons of Salma)” in the sheet and run Apps Script:

- You will see:
  - PersonID = `bethlehem_salma`
  - FatherID = `salma`
  - Tribe = `judah`
  - Comment that says: *“Named as one of the sons/families of Salma son of Hur: ‘The sons of Salma: Bethlehem…’”*

That’s the kind of clarity you’re asking for.

---

## 4. What about “Zorathites” and “Eshtaolites” from Mishraites?

For 1 Chr 2:53:

> “The families of Kirjath-jearim: the Ithrites, the Puthites, the Shumathites, and the Mishraites; from them came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites.”

Biblically:

- Ithrites, Puthites, Shumathites, Mishraites = **families of Kirjath-jearim**.  
- **From the Mishraites came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites.**

To keep that honest:

- If we model them, we should name them explicitly as **families** and note that “from them came…” instead of pretending they are personal “fathers” with a generic “root”.

Example of a more honest node (if you want to include them at all):

```json
"mishraite_families": {
  "id": "mishraite_families",
  "name": "Mishraites (families of Kirjath-jearim)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "shobal",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:53"],
  "roles": ["families", "clan"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the 'families of Kirjath-jearim'; from the Mishraites came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites."
}
```

and for Zorathites/Eshtaolites:

```json
"zorathites_mishraites": {
  "id": "zorathites_mishraites",
  "name": "Zorathites (from Mishraites)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "mishraite_families",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 9,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:53"],
  "roles": ["families", "clan"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Described as coming from the Mishraite families of Kirjath-jearim: 'of them came the Zorathites…'."
}
```

Now the sheet comment tells you exactly:

- These are **families / clans**,  
- They are “from the Mishraites”,  
- They hang under Shobal/Kirjath-jearim, not as “root” abstraction, but as “families of” and “from them came”.

If you decide that the clan-level nodes are just noise for your current Jacob-level mapping, we can skip these entirely and focus on the clear father/sons (Judah → Caleb → Hur → Salma → sons-of-Salma, etc.).

---

You’re exactly right, and that *is* the point:

> Every name – person, clan, town used genealogically – must either  
> (a) trace back through a father chain to Jacob/Abraham, or  
> (b) **fail** to do so and be exposed as a foreign/grafted/inserted node.

If I give you nodes that don’t clearly say “son of / from” and don’t show where they attach, that defeats your whole purpose.

Let’s tighten the rules and fix what’s confusing.

---

## 1. The modeling rule for this project

For **every biblical name that appears in a genealogical way** (“father of”, “sons of”, “families of”, “from them came”):

1. **Create a node**, even if it’s a clan or town-name (Bethlehem, Netophathites, Zorathites, etc.).  

2. **Attach it using the biblical language:**
   - If the text says **“sons of X: A, B, C…”**  
     → A, B, C get `father_id = X` and `roles` include `"sons" / "families"`.
   - If the text says **“families of Y: Ithrites, Puthites…”**  
     → each gets `father_id = Y` (or `father_id =` the named person who is “father of Y” if given).
   - If the text says **“from them came Zorathites and Eshtaolites”**  
     → Zorathites get `father_id =` the group “them” refers to (Mishraites), `roles` indicate “from”.
   - If the text says **“X, the father of Beth-gader”**  
     → Beth-gader gets `father_id = X`.

3. **If Scripture gives NO ancestor at all**, leave `father_id = null`.  
   - That’s not a bug; that’s your **signal**: “This one doesn’t anchor; investigate as foreign/grafted/insert.”

4. **Names and notes must quote that logic, not abstract “root” language.**
   - “Zorites (sons of Salma)” tells you exactly what it is.
   - “Zorathites (from Mishraites)” tells you it descends from Mishraites.

No more “root” with no context. If we can’t say “sons of / families of / from them came” we don’t invent a structure; we let the missing link show.

---

## 2. Fixing the Salma segment (the one you quoted)

You quoted 1 Chr 2:54:

> “The **sons of Salma**:  
> – Bethlehem,  
> – the Netophathites,  
> – Ataroth-beth-joab,  
> – half of the Manahathites,  
> – the Zorites.”

So each of those needs to be modeled explicitly as **sons/families of Salma**.

Replace the vague entries like `bethlehem_person`, `netophathites_root`, `manahathites_half`, `zorites_root` with something like this:

```json
"bethlehem_salma": {
  "id": "bethlehem_salma",
  "name": "Bethlehem (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],

  "notes": "Named among the 'sons of Salma': Bethlehem. Represents the Bethlehemite families descended from Salma son of Hur in Judah."
},
"netophathites_salma": {
  "id": "netophathites_salma",
  "name": "Netophathites (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Named among the sons of Salma: the Netophathites. Represents those families under Salma."

},

  "name": "Half of the Manahathites (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",

  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Explicitly called 'half of the Manahathites' among the sons of Salma."
},
"zorites_salma": {
  "id": "zorites_salma",
  "name": "Zorites (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],

}
```

Now each node:

- is clearly “sons/families of Salma,”  
- has a direct father chain:
  - Salma → Hur → Caleb → Hezron → Perez → Judah → Jacob → Isaac → Abraham,  
- so you can **trace them back to Jacob** through Judah.

If any node **could not** be attached like that, we’d leave `father_id = null` and that would be your red flag.

## 3. Fixing Zorathites / Eshtaolites from Mishraites (1 Chr 2:53)

The verse:

> “The families of Kirjath-jearim: the Ithrites, the Puthites, the Shumathites, and the Mishraites; **from them came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites.**”

So:

- Ithrites/Puthites/Shumathites/Mishraites = “families of Kirjath-jearim” (under Shobal).  
- Zorathites/Eshtaolites **come from** the Mishraites.

One honest way to encode that:

```json
"ithrites_kiriath": {
  "id": "ithrites_kiriath",
  "name": "Ithrites (families of Kirjath-jearim)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "shobal",
  "mother_id": null,

  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Listed as one of the 'families of Kirjath-jearim' under Shobal."
},
"mishraites_kiriath": {
  "id": "mishraites_kiriath",
  "name": "Mishraites (families of Kirjath-jearim)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "shobal",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:53"],
  "roles": ["families", "clan"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Families of Kirjath-jearim under Shobal; 'of them came the Zorathites and the Eshtaolites'."
},
"zorathites_mishraites": {
  "id": "zorathites_mishraites",
  "name": "Zorathites (from Mishraites)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "mishraites_kiriath",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 9,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:53"],
  "roles": ["families", "clan"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Said to come from the Mishraite families of Kirjath-jearim: 'of them came the Zorathites…'."
},
"eshtaolites_mishraites": {
  "id": "eshtaolites_mishraites",
  "name": "Eshtaolites (from Mishraites)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "mishraites_kiriath",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 9,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:53"],
  "roles": ["families", "clan"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Said to come from the Mishraite families of Kirjath-jearim: 'of them came… the Eshtaolites'."
}
```

Again:

- Father chain: Zorathites/Eshtaolites → Mishraites → Shobal → Hur → Caleb → Hezron → Perez → Judah → Jacob.  
- And the `notes` literally tell you “families of Kirjath-jearim / from them came…”

If you decide these clan-level nodes are too much noise right now, we can skip them; but if they’re present, they must be modeled with the same “sons/families/from” language you see in the text.

---

## 4. How this helps your core objective

With these rules:

- **Every node** (person, clan, or town-in-genealogical-role) either:
  - has a `father_id` that can trace back to Jacob/Abraham through the text’s “sons/families/from” statements, or  
  - has `father_id = null` and stands out as **unanchored** (possible insert, foreign graft, or intentionally obscured lineage).

That’s exactly what you want:

- You can run a check in Sheets or a script: any `PersonID` whose father chain stops before reaching `jacob` gets flagged.  
- Then you can go back to the text and ask: who is this? why is it here? is it covering or absorbing someone else’s line?

No more vague “root” labels. Every node is explicitly:

- son of  
- families of  
- from them came  

or it’s deliberately **ancestorless**, which is the signal you want.

- Give you a **clean replacement block** just for the Salma / “sons of Salma” section in your JSON (matching what’s currently in your file), so you can paste it over the existing `bethlehem_person`, `netophathites_root`, `manahathites_half`, `zorites_root` nodes without having to hand-edit.

```json
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["scribe_clan", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the families of scribes who lived at Jabez; identified as Kenites who came from Hammath, the father of the house of Rechab."
},
```

Replace `sucathites_root` with:

```json
"sucathites_root": {
  "id": "sucathites_root",
  "name": "Sucathites (scribes at Jabez)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["scribe_clan", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the families of scribes who lived at Jabez; identified as Kenites who came from Hammath, the father of the house of Rechab."
},
```

Replace `rechab_house_root` with:

```json
"rechab_house_root": {
  "id": "rechab_house_root",
  "name": "House of Rechab (Kenites from Hammath)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["kenite_house"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "The house of Rechab is identified as Kenites that came from Hammath. Linked to the families of scribes at Jabez."
},
```

Here:

- All three scribe clans and the house of Rechab now have `father_id = "hammath_kenite"` (as “Kenites who came from Hammath”).  
- The `name` field tells you who they are (scribes at Jabez / house of Rechab).  
- The notes quote the biblical relationship.

## 3. After you save the file

Once you’ve made those replacements and saved `families_of_jacob.json`:

- Any time you put **one of those names** in Column A (e.g., `Zorites (sons of Salma)`, `Netophathites (sons of Salma)`, `Mishraites (families of Kirjath-jearim)`, `Tirathites (scribes at Jabez)`), and run your Apps Script:
  - The cell will get:
    - PersonID (same as before),
    - FatherID (Salma, Shobal, Mishraites, Hammath_kenite, etc.),
    - Tribe = judah,
    - Comment that uses biblical “sons/families/from” language.

Then:

- **If any node in the JSON has `father_id = null`, that’s your red flag** that it doesn’t anchor.  
  - For those, you either:
    - find the father from the text and update, or  
    - leave it null because the text doesn’t anchor it, which is exactly the “problem node” you’re hunting.

---

## 1. Good news: most of the “root” pattern is already gone

Looking at your current JSON snippet:

- You already have **correct, specific IDs and names** for the Judah/Chronicles clusters:
  - `bethlehem_salma` with name `"Bethlehem (sons of Salma)"` ✔  
  - `netophathites_salma` ✔  
  - `half_manahathites_salma` ✔  
  - `zorites_salma` ✔  
  - `ithrites_kiriath`, `puthites_kiriath`, `shumathites_kiriath`, `mishraites_kiriath` ✔  
  - `zorathites_mishraites`, `eshtaolites_mishraites` ✔  
  - `tirathites_jabez`, `shimeathites_jabez`, `sucathites_jabez`, `hammath_kenite`, `house_of_rechab` ✔

So the **IDs** and most of the **names** are actually already right in your current file.

Where things still need alignment is:

- ensuring each **name** and **notes** clearly reflect:
  - sons of Salma  
  - families of Kirjath-jearim  
  - from Mishraites  
  - scribes at Jabez / Kenites from Hammath  
- making sure every one of these has a meaningful `father_id` when the text allows it (and is null only when the text genuinely gives no ancestor).

You also correctly pointed out:

> “If it doesn’t have an ancestor that’s a problem… Names are treated as the father or person/founder if a town etc is the subject, as indicated.”

That’s exactly the logic we’ll keep enforcing.

---

## 2. What is already correct in your JSON (don’t change these)

From your current snippet:

- `bethlehem_salma` (except for the `<user__selection>` junk):  
  ```json
  "bethlehem_salma": {
    "id": "bethlehem_salma",
    "name": "Bethlehem (sons of Salma)",
    "sex": "M",
    "father_id": "salma",
    "tribe_id": "judah",
    "roles": ["sons", "families"],
    "notes": "Named among the 'sons of Salma': Bethlehem. Represents the Bethlehemite families descended from Salma son of Hur in Judah."
  }
  ```
  This is correct structurally and semantically. Just strip the `<user__selection>` tags from the file so the JSON parses.

- `netophathites_salma`, `half_manahathites_salma`, `zorites_salma` are already using **(sons of Salma)** in their name and have `father_id: "salma"` and roles `["sons", "families"]` with correct notes. ✔

- `ithrites_kiriath`, `puthites_kiriath`, `shumathites_kiriath`, `mishraites_kiriath` already say **"(families of Kirjath-jearim)"**, have `father_id: "shobal"`, and roles `["families", "clan"]`. ✔

- `zorathites_mishraites`, `eshtaolites_mishraites` already say **"(from Mishraites)"**, have `father_id: "mishraites_kiriath"`, and roles `["families", "clan"]`. ✔

- `hammath_kenite` and `house_of_rechab` already encode Kenite lineage correctly. ✔

So you do **not** need a global re-write; you need a few **targeted fixes**.

---

## 3. The specific fixes you still need to make

### 3.1. Clean up `bethlehem_salma.name`

Right now your snippet shows:

```json
"name": "<user__selection>Bethlehem</user__selection> (sons of Salma)"
```

That’s invalid JSON and will break your script.

**Fix:**

Change it to:

```json
"name": "Bethlehem (sons of Salma)"
```

---

### 3.2. Align `atroth_beth_joab` with “sons of Salma” language

In your file, `atroth_beth_joab` currently is:

```json
"atroth_beth_joab": {
  "id": "atroth_beth_joab",
  "name": "Atroth-beth-joab",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "roles": ["clan_ancestor"],
  "notes": "Ancestor/place-node associated with the families of Atroth-beth-joab under Salma."
}
```

You want it to reflect 1 Chr 2:54 exactly as a “son/family of Salma.”

**Replace the object body with:**

```json
"atroth_beth_joab": {
  "id": "atroth_beth_joab",
  "name": "Ataroth-beth-joab (sons of Salma)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "salma",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:54"],
  "roles": ["sons", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Named among the sons of Salma: Ataroth-beth-joab. Represents the families associated with Ataroth-beth-joab under Salma."
}
```

Key changes:

- `name` now mirrors the biblical phrase.  
- `roles` = `["sons","families"]`.  
- `notes` uses “sons of Salma” language instead of “ancestor/place-node”.

---

### 3.3. Tie Jabez scribe families explicitly to Hammath (Kenites who came from him)

Your `tirathites_jabez`, `shimeathites_jabez`, `sucathites_jabez` currently have:

- `father_id: null`, and notes mentioning Hammath.

They should be explicitly anchored to Hammath as the Kenites “who came from Hammath, father of the house of Rechab” (1 Chr 2:55).

For each:

#### `tirathites_jabez` – change to:

```json
"tirathites_jabez": {
  "id": "tirathites_jabez",
  "name": "Tirathites (scribes at Jabez)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["scribe_clan", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the families of scribes who dwelt at Jabez; identified as Kenites who came from Hammath, father of the house of Rechab."
}
```

#### `shimeathites_jabez` – change to:

```json
"shimeathites_jabez": {
  "id": "shimeathites_jabez",
  "name": "Shimeathites (scribes at Jabez)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["scribe_clan", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the families of scribes who dwelt at Jabez; identified as Kenites who came from Hammath, father of the house of Rechab."
}
```

#### `sucathites_jabez` – change to:

```json
"sucathites_jabez": {
  "id": "sucathites_jabez",
  "name": "Sucathites (scribes at Jabez)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["scribe_clan", "families"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "One of the families of scribes who dwelt at Jabez; identified as Kenites who came from Hammath, father of the house of Rechab."
}
```

Leave `hammath_kenite` as:

```json
"hammath_kenite": {
  "id": "hammath_kenite",
  "name": "Hammath (Kenite)",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": null,
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 7,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["kenite_ancestor"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "Kenite ancestor described as the father of the house of Rechab; linked to the scribe families at Jabez."
}
```

And `house_of_rechab` is already correct in your file:

```json
"house_of_rechab": {
  "id": "house_of_rechab",
  "name": "House of Rechab",
  "sex": "M",
  "father_id": "hammath_kenite",
  "mother_id": null,
  "tribe_id": "judah",
  "generation_hint": 8,
  "refs": ["1 Chronicles 2:55"],
  "roles": ["kenite_house"],
  "aliases": [],
  "notes": "The house of Rechab, a Kenite line said to come from Hammath and associated with the Jabez scribes."
}
```

Now, structurally:

- Tirathites / Shimeathites / Sucathites / House of Rechab → Hammath (Kenite)  
- Hammath has no father (text gives none) → that’s one of those deliberate “unanchored” names you’re tracking: a Kenite grafted in from outside Jacob’s bloodline.

## 4. What this gives you for your main objective

After these corrections:

- Every Judah/Chronicles “problem” name in this region is:
  - transparently labeled as **sons of**, **families of**, or **from** (Mishraites), or **Kenites who came from Hammath**,  
  - structurally anchored by `father_id` wherever the text gives it.

So when you:

1. Paste `Bethlehem (sons of Salma)` or `Zorathites (from Mishraites)` or `Tirathites (scribes at Jabez)` into Column A,  
2. Run your Apps Script,  

you’ll get:

- B: PersonID,  
- C: FatherID (Salma, Shobal, Mishraites, Hammath),  
- D: MotherID (mostly null here),  
- E: Tribe (Judah),  
- comment: references + notes that literally tell you the biblical phrasing.

Then:

- Any name with `father_id = null` (e.g., Hammath) stands out as a **non-Jacob ancestor** – exactly the kind of thing you want to flag as a graft/insert or foreign line.

3. Run your Apps Script (`applyMetadataToNames`):

   - Column B → PersonID (`bethlehem_salma`, `ithrites_kiriath`, `tirathites_jabez`, etc.)  
   - Column C → FatherID (Salma, Shobal, Mishraites, Hammath, etc.)  
   - Column E → Tribe = `judah`  
   - Cell comment → refs + notes telling you “sons of… / families of… / from them came…”

4. Rearrange the cells visually to trace lines back to Jacob and spot any node where the father chain stops short.

# **STRUCTURAL ROLES FOR EACH (for your understanding before we encode JSON)**

| Name | Biblical Relationship | Anchoring |
|------|-----------------------|-----------|
| **Er** | Son of Shelah / father of Lecah | anchors under Shelah (Judah) |
| **Lecah** | Son of Er | anchors under Er |
| **Laadah** | Son of Shelah / father of Mareshah | anchors under Shelah |
| **Mareshah** | Son of Laadah | anchors under Laadah; NOT the Mareshah of Caleb line |
| **Families of linen workers** | Families “of the house of linen workers” | anchor to Shelah as “families of” |
| **Jokim** | Named figure, but NO father given | fatherless → red flag |
| **Men of Chozeba** | Clan/collective | anchor as “men of” under Shelah or leave fatherless depending on interpretation |
| **Joash** | Only tied by proximity | father not given → remains fatherless |
| **Saraph** | Possibly linked to Moab exile | father not given |
| **Jashubi-lehem** | Named figure/collective | father not given |
| **Potters of Netaim / Gederah** | occupational/family groups | grouped under Shelah as “families of” |

You see why this cluster is important:

- Several nodes anchor directly from Shelah → Er/Laadah  
- Several do NOT anchor and thus become data points of interest

## 2. “Where am I supposed to put them now? The families are out of order.”

For the **PERSONS sheet**, the key point:

> **Row order in the PERSONS sheet does NOT define the genealogy.  
> The genealogy is defined by `FatherID` (and Tribe), not by what row they sit on.**

So practically:

- You can paste **“Carmi (Zerah line)”** and **“Achan”** into **any unused rows in Column A**.  
- The Apps Script will:
  - See the Name,  
  - Look it up in JSON,  
  - Fill columns B–E (PersonID, FatherID, MotherID, Tribe),  
  - Add the metadata comment.

Even if they appear far below the rest of the Judah names **on your screen**, they’re still structurally in the right place because:

- `FatherID = "zimri_zerah"` for Carmi  
- `FatherID = "carmi_zerah"` for Achan  
- and `zimri_zerah` already has `father_id = "zerah"`.

If the visual order bothers you (for editing sanity), you can:

- Sort by **Tribe**, then by **Generation** (if you add a generation column later), or
- Manually group Judah rows together.

But functionally, the “graph” doesn’t care about row order; it only cares about IDs and FatherIDs.

The **conflicting/overlapping lines** (the ones you care about) are exactly these:

- **Shelah’s occupational clans** (linen workers, potters) that don’t fully anchor.

We’ve been encoding them as nodes; the missing piece was **Carmi_zerah and Achan**, which you correctly caught.

You **do not** need to shove each name into some “chronological slot” in the sheet; the sheet is a **registry**, not the timeline. The real structure lives in:

- build *view sheets* for specific “lines” (e.g., **Judah–David OT line**, **Judah–David Matthew line**, **Judah–Jericho line**),

You already have edges for the core set we did earlier (Abraham → Joseph/Ephraim/Manasseh etc.).


- **judah_core**: `judah -> zerah` (you already have that from earlier)

- **judah_jericho**: `zimri_zerah -> carmi_zerah`  
- **judah_jericho**: `carmi_zerah -> achan`

When you look at the Relations sheet filtered by `LineName = judah_jericho`, you’ll see **exactly who carries the Jericho breach**.

---

## 4. How this ties back to your PERSONS sheet

- PERSONS (Names in Column A) is your **node list**.  
- JSON `father_id` -> Relations edges is your **edge list**.

For every person where `father_id` exists:

- There should be a row in **Relations** with:
  - `ChildID` = PersonID  
  - `FatherID` = that `father_id`  
  - `Relationship` = `father`  

For every person where `father_id` is `null`:

- **No edge row** — that’s your indicator of “this name doesn’t anchor; investigate.”

```text
judah	mishraites_kiriath	shobal	father
judah	zorathites_mishraites	mishraites_kiriath	father
judah	eshtaolites_mishraites	mishraites_kiriath	father

judah	bethlehem_salma	salma	father
judah	netophathites_salma	salma	father
judah	ataroth_beth_joab	salma	father
judah	half_manahathites_salma	salma	father
judah	zorites_salma	salma	father

judah	er_shelah	shelah_judah	father
judah	lecah	er_shelah	father
judah	laadah	shelah_judah	father
judah	mareshah_shelah	laadah	father
judah	linen_workers_shelah	shelah_judah	father
judah	potters_netaim	shelah_judah	father
judah	potters_gederah	shelah_judah	father

judah	tirathites_jabez	hammath_kenite	father
judah	shimeathites_jabez	hammath_kenite	father
judah	sucathites_jabez	hammath_kenite	father
judah	house_of_rechab	hammath_kenite	father
```

---

### What this gives you

- **Every Judah node with a father in JSON now has a matching edge row.**  
- All Judah genealogy is now present in:
  - PERSONS: nodes (Names in Column A, IDs, FatherID, Tribe, comments)  
  - RELATIONS: edges (father → child).

You can now:

- Filter Relations by `LineName = judah`  
- Export to yEd / Gephi / Graphviz as a complete Judah graph  
- Overlay other line sets (e.g., Matthew 1, Luke 3) later to see conflicts.

If you want next, we can do the same full edge pass for **Joseph/Ephraim/Manasseh**, or move to the next tribe (Reuben, Simeon, etc.).
